capital reopens after months of gang violence, helping to ease humanitarian crisis | CBC News Loaded</div><main class="feed-content content" id="content"><!--$--><div class="detail detailBody pageComponent"><div class="detailBodyContainer withSidebar"><div class="withFlex"><div class="detailMainCol sclt-storycontent" id="detailContent"><!--$--><span class="detail-link-label sclt-storySectionLink"><a class="" href="/news/world"><span>World</span></a></span><!--/$--><h1 class="detailHeadline" lang="en" data-cy="detailHeadline">Airport in Haiti&#x27;s capital reopens after months of gang violence, helping to ease humanitarian crisis</h1><div class="detailSummary">Haiti&#x27;s main international airport reopened on Monday for the first time in nearly three months after relentless gang violence forced authorities to close it to all traffic in early March.</div><h2 class="deck" lang="en">Powerful armed groups have controlled much of Port-au-Prince for nearly 3 months</h2><!--$--><div class="byline"><figure class="imageMedia author-image full"><div class="placeholder"><img loading="lazy" alt="" src="https://i.cbc.ca/1.4288247.1574090018!/fileImage/httpImage/image.jpg_gen/derivatives/square_140/associated-press-logo.jpg" data-cy="author-image-img"/></div></figure><div class="bylineDetails"><span class="authorText" data-cy="author-text"><a class="" href="/news/world/author/danica-coto-1.4363353">Danica Coto</a></span> <span class="bullet"> · </span>The Associated Press<!-- --> <span class="bullet"> · </span><time class="timeStamp" dateTime="2024-05-20T18:46:22.624Z">Posted: May 20, 2024 2:46 PM EDT | Last Updated: May 20</time></div></div><!--/$--><!--$--><div data-cy="storyWrapper"><!--$--><figure class="imageMedia leadmedia-story full"><div class="placeholder"><img alt="A blurred image of a woman on a street carrying a large, red bowl on her head as she walks past a welcome sign, in English and French, for an airport. Debris, garbage and clothing are scattered on the street below the sign." src="https://i.cbc.ca/1.7209418.1716226668!/cpImage/httpImage/image.jpg_gen/derivatives/16x9_780/haiti-violence-port-au-prince-airport-march-2024.jpg" data-cy="leadmedia-story-img" fetchpriority="high"/></div><figcaption class="image-caption">The airport in Haiti&#x27;s capital, Port-au-Prince, has been closed since March amid gang violence and a power struggle with the government of former prime minister Ariel Henry. <!-- --> <!-- -->(Odelyn Joseph/The Associated Press)</figcaption></figure><!--/$--><div class="engagement-widgets"><div class="share"><h2 class="a11y">Social Sharing</h2><div class="viafoura"></div></div></div><div class="story"><p>Haiti&#x27;s main international airport reopened on Monday for the first time in nearly three months after relentless gang violence forced authorities to close it to all traffic in early March.</p><p>The reopening of the Toussaint Louverture International Airport in the capital, Port-au-Prince, is expected to help ease a critical shortage of medication and other basic supplies, since the country&#x27;s main seaport remains paralyzed.</p><p>However, only Sunrise Airways, a local carrier, is flying in and out of Port-au-Prince for now. U.S.-based airlines are not expected to start doing so until late May or early June.</p><p>The first Sunrise Airways flight, bound for Miami, was scheduled to depart at 2:30 p.m. ET.</p><p>Before Monday&#x27;s reopening, the sole airport operating in Haiti was located in the north coastal city of Cap-Haïtien.</p><div><ul class="similarLinks"><li class="similarListItem"><a href="https://www.cbc.ca/news/world/haiti-violence-ariel-henry-explained-1.7135709" class="similarLink" text="What&#x27;s behind the violent power struggle in Haiti — and what experts say Canada should do about it" flag="" data-contentid=""><span class="similarLinkText">What&#x27;s behind the violent power struggle in Haiti — and what experts say Canada should do about it</span></a></li></ul></div><p>However, it was out of reach for many seeking to flee the country since the roads leading from Port-au-Prince to Cap-Haïtien are controlled by gangs that have opened fire on cars and buses passing through.</p><p>As a result, the Canadian and U.S. governments evacuated citizens and permanent residents by helicopter from elsewhere in Port-au-Prince, as did non-profit organizations, as powerful gangs laid siege to parts of the capital.</p><div><strong><em>WATCH</em> | <em>CBC News in Haiti&#x27;s capital, where gangs control much of the city:</em></strong><span><span class="mediaEmbed"><div class="player-placeholder-ui-container "><div class="player-placeholder-video-ui" title="CBC News gets rare access to Port-au-Prince as Haiti Port-au-Prince to witness the cataclysmic humanitarian crisis and efforts to bring food and aid to millions of Haitians.</span></span></span></div><h2>Capital gripped by violence</h2><p>The attacks began on Feb. 29, with gunmen seizing control of police stations, opening fire on the Port-au-Prince airport and storming Haiti&#x27;s two biggest prisons, freeing more than 4,000 inmates.</p><p>Gangs have since directed their attacks on previously peaceful communities, leaving thousands homeless.</p><div><figure class="imageMedia image full"><div class="placeholder"><img loading="lazy" alt="People walk among a number of burned out cars." srcSet="https://i.cbc.ca/1.7160524.1716230583!/fileImage/httpImage/image.jpg_gen/derivatives/original_300/haiti-violence.jpg 620px) 620px,(max-width: 780px) 780px,(max-width: 1180px) 1180px" src="https://i.cbc.ca/1.7160524.1716230583!/fileImage/httpImage/image.jpg_gen/derivatives/original_780/haiti-violence.jpg" style="aspect-ratio:1.6103896103896105" data-cy="image-img"/></div><figcaption class="image-caption">People look for salvageable pieces from burned cars at a mechanic shop that was set on fire during violence by armed gangs, in Port-au-Prince on March 25.<!-- --> <!-- -->(Odelyn Joseph/The Associated Press)</figcaption></figure></div><p>More than 2,500 people have been killed or injured in Haiti from January to March, an increase of more than 50 per cent compared with the same period last year, according to the United Nations.</p><p>The attack on the airport left then-prime minister Ariel Henry, who was on an official trip to Kenya at the time, locked out of Haiti. He has since resigned, and a transitional presidential council is seeking a new prime minister for Haiti.</p><div><ul class="similarLinks"><li class="similarListItem"><a href="https://www.cbc.ca/news/world/haiti-ariel-henry-resigns-transitional-council-1.7184794" class="similarLink" text="Haiti&#x27;s prime minister resigns, transitional leadership takes over as gang violence persists" flag="" data-contentid=""><span class="similarLinkText">Haiti&#x27;s prime minister resigns, transitional leadership takes over as gang violence persists</span></a></li></ul></div><p>The council is also tasked with selecting a new cabinet and organizing general elections.</p><p>In recent weeks, U.S. military planes have landed at the Port-au-Prince airport with supplies, including medication and hydration fluids — as well as civilian contractors to help Haiti prepare for the arrival of foreign forces expected to help quell violence unleashed by gangs, who control 80 per cent of the capital.</p><div><strong><em>WATCH</em> | <em>People of Port-au-Prince reliant on humanitarian assistance amid security rely on humanitarian aid for almost everything. Officials in Haiti are anxiously waiting for a multinational force to arrive and hopefully restore order.</span></span></span></div><h2>Foreign police officers on the way</h2><p>On Sunday, Korir Sing&#x27;oei, Kenya&#x27;s principal secretary for foreign affairs, said a plan to deploy police officers from the East African country was in its final stages.</p><p>&quot;I can tell you for sure that that deployment will happen in the next few days, few weeks,&quot; he said. Sing&#x27;oei added that &quot;there is no chance at all&quot; that Kenyan President William Ruto will visit Haiti.</p><p>Ruto was scheduled to depart Kenya on Sunday for an official four-day visit to the U.S., where he is expected to meet President Joe Biden.</p><div><ul class="similarLinks"><li class="similarListItem"><a href="https://www.cbc.ca/news/caf-members-deploy-jamaica-haiti-mission-1.7159885" class="similarLink" text="Canadian Forces personnel deploy to Jamaica to train troops for Haiti mission" flag="" data-contentid=""><span class="similarLinkText">Canadian Forces personnel deploy to Jamaica to train troops for Haiti mission</span></a></li></ul><ul class="similarLinks"><li class="similarListItem"><a href="https://www.cbc.ca/news/politics/haiti-canada-trudeau-rae-gang-violence-1.7145349" class="similarLink" text="The world is sending soldiers back to Haiti — this time without Canada&#x27;s help" flag="Analysis" data-contentid=""><div class="label flag"><span class="labelText external">Analysis</span></div><span class="similarLinkText">The world is sending soldiers back to Haiti — this time without Canada&#x27;s help</span></a></li></ul></div><p>In March, Kenya and Haiti signed agreements to try to salvage a plan for the African country to deploy 1,000 police officers to the troubled Caribbean nation to help bring an end to the violence.</p><p>Other countries expected to back up the Kenyan forces include the Bahamas, Barbados, Benin, Chad and Bangladesh. It wasn&#x27;t immediately clear when those forces would arrive.</p><div><strong><em>WATCH</em> | <em>Uneasy calm in Haiti&#x27;s capital as transitional government struggles to restore
